<div id="review_1429570903" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1429570903" />
    <a title="Elaine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13060256-elaine"><img alt="Elaine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1410409969p2/13060256.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1429570903?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elaine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elaine" href="/user/show/13060256-elaine">Elaine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1429570903" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2842392493313112712">What I really like about Isabel Allende is her ability to create families that, despite their quirks and off the wall characters, are so well drawn that they feel real and she has done it again here with the Bellasco family. By the end of the read I almost felt as if I too was a part of this dynasty. <br/><br/>The story is mostly set in a San Fransisco Bay area residential complex for the elderly. I loved this setting – an old people’s complex with a clientele drawn from the hippie generation. These peopl</span>
  <span id="freeText2842392493313112712" style="display:none">What I really like about Isabel Allende is her ability to create families that, despite their quirks and off the wall characters, are so well drawn that they feel real and she has done it again here with the Bellasco family. By the end of the read I almost felt as if I too was a part of this dynasty. <br /><br />The story is mostly set in a San Fransisco Bay area residential complex for the elderly. I loved this setting – an old people’s complex with a clientele drawn from the hippie generation. These people are, by and large, fairly independent with access to all their medical requirements, traditional and non traditional, including marijuana. Irina works at the complex and our story begins when one of the residents, charismatic and enigmatic Alma Bellasco takes a shine to her and offers her extra work as a secretary. <br /><br />As the two women get closer, we find out more about them. We gradually discover why Irina doesn’t want to get close to anyone and who or what she is hiding from but the main story is that of Alma’s life. This is a love story which spans a lifetime, one of destiny, separations and heartache. Can a woman from a pampered society background have a relationship with Ichimei, the son of the Japanese gardener? They first meet as children and quickly become best friends but that friendship will be torn asunder during World War II when Ichimei and his family are interred by the Americans along with other Japanese residents in the US. I didn’t really know too much about these internments before I read this book and I have to say the sections set in Topaz, the internment camp do come as something of an eye opener. <br /><br />Ichimei and his family believe in honour and respect and the Bellascos are philanthropists with the two families being tied to each other by a mutual bond of honour throughout the decades. As their story progress you realise this is not just the love story between Alma and Ichimei, there are other loves in this read and I marvelled at the way the author showed that it is possible to love different people at the same time and in different ways. It is a story that is not as predictable as you think and I did get quite a few surprises during the read. I adored Alma and her capacity to love the people in her life in a read that is quirky and moving at the same time, and one in which I really got drawn into. The best way that I can describe this read is to say that for me, it “feels” like Isabel Allende from the first page. I hope that makes sense. Many thanks to the publishers via Netgalley for the review copy.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2842392493313112712" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1361041560" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1361041560" />
    <a title="DeB MaRtEnS" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9827967-deb-martens"><img alt="DeB MaRtEnS" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593294620p2/9827967.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1361041560?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="DeB MaRtEnS" class="user" itemprop="url" name="DeB MaRtEnS" href="/user/show/9827967-deb-martens">DeB MaRtEnS</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9827967-deb-martens?shelf=feeling-it">feeling-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9827967-deb-martens?shelf=aplus-2016">aplus-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9827967-deb-martens?shelf=memorably-good">memorably-good</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9827967-deb-martens?shelf=love-finds-a-way">love-finds-a-way</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9827967-deb-martens?shelf=sagas">sagas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9827967-deb-martens?shelf=magic-realism-fantasy">magic-realism-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9827967-deb-martens?shelf=dramatic-fiction">dramatic-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1361041560" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer512003946354218377">A quiet, contemplative book... A look at the life of Alma Mendel, sent as a child to live with her aunt and uncle in San Francisco. Her Jewish parents are never able to find their way to her from their native Poland, victims of Nazi atrocities. Isaac and Lillian Blasco, her relatives, whose wealth increases with no diminishing of their innate kindness..., their grandson, Nathaniel, beloved and steady, loyal....Ichimei Fukuda, gardener's son, Japanese internee, dreamer. Seth, Alma's grandson, a m</span>
  <span id="freeText512003946354218377" style="display:none">A quiet, contemplative book... A look at the life of Alma Mendel, sent as a child to live with her aunt and uncle in San Francisco. Her Jewish parents are never able to find their way to her from their native Poland, victims of Nazi atrocities. Isaac and Lillian Blasco, her relatives, whose wealth increases with no diminishing of their innate kindness..., their grandson, Nathaniel, beloved and steady, loyal....Ichimei Fukuda, gardener's son, Japanese internee, dreamer. Seth, Alma's grandson, a man graced with Belasco compassion... Alma is at the centre, bracketed by unconditional love. <br /><br />Unconditional love. What would you be, if it had held you all of your life? Alma was uncompromising, created a life to suit her talents, travelled the world to explore creativity, had choices and took them bravely, lived realistically yet freely... And in her eighties, she made another choice, to move to a senior's facility, Lark House. She cast off the burden of possessing most material goods but her papers and photos needed order. <br /><br />In counterpoint to Alma is Irina. She is Seth's age, an immigrant from Moldavia, raised in abject poverty by her beloved maternal grandparents. She once understood love, and attaches its memory to the elderly who are her clients at Lark House. Irina was sent to join a mother she barely knew, when she was ten, for a better life. No choice, no love, choking loss...<br /><br />Allende brings them together in Lark House, another house of spirits... They say it is haunted; Irina sees her grandparents in the giant trees, the seniors sense the otherworldly and consider their souls and take up or renew a religion. Seth and Irina collate Alma's papers and her memories. The saga of lives lived around Alma unfold. <br /><br />In the folds, there was always Ichimei, or Ichi, first the boy who Alma loved and then the man. The great love, soul love, recorded in Ichi's letters. Fiercely protected, that most vulnerable tender place which privately sustained her. If lost... She could be an Irina. <br /><br />I reflected on the mercy of being exposed to people who have known unconditional love throughout their lives. The acceptance, the forever knowledge that love is almost corporeal, a fact so familiar that it goes unrecognized by the recipients - and in this novel so tenderly described in the stories which surrounded Alma and Ichi- and the web of healing that results, for wounded souls like Irina. <br /><br />This is a thoughtful, pensive Isabel Allende. I really do approve.</span>
  <a data-text-id="512003946354218377" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_1278118284" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1278118284" />
    <a title="Rebecca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5875398-rebecca"><img alt="Rebecca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599578317p2/5875398.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1278118284?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca" href="/user/show/5875398-rebecca">Rebecca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5875398-rebecca?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5875398-rebecca?shelf=war-fiction">war-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5875398-rebecca?shelf=lit-in-translation">lit-in-translation</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1278118284" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3321192754752128047"><b>(3.5)</b> Allende is a wonderful storyteller. This isn’t up to the level of her South American novels (e.g. <i>The House of the Spirits</i>), and in elaborating both Alma’s and Irina’s stories there’s a bit too much <b>telling</b> rather than <b>showing</b>, but I thoroughly enjoyed the book all the same – I devoured it in just a few days. Allende is sensitive to both the process of aging and the various strategies for dealing with traumatic events from the past. If you’re interested in exploring the internment of Ameri</span>
  <span id="freeText3321192754752128047" style="display:none"><b>(3.5)</b> Allende is a wonderful storyteller. This isn’t up to the level of her South American novels (e.g. <i>The House of the Spirits</i>), and in elaborating both Alma’s and Irina’s stories there’s a bit too much <b>telling</b> rather than <b>showing</b>, but I thoroughly enjoyed the book all the same – I devoured it in just a few days. Allende is sensitive to both the process of aging and the various strategies for dealing with traumatic events from the past. If you’re interested in exploring the internment of America’s Japanese during World War II, two other novels that also feature this shameful historical episode are <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/302155846" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>The Buddha in the Attic</i>
</a> by Julia Otsuka and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/893407597" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>China Dolls</i>
</a> by Lisa See.</span>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="~Bookishly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="~Bookishly" href="/user/show/28323108-bookishly">~Bookishly</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25275996-the-japanese-lover">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28323108-bookishly?shelf=bleh">bleh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28323108-bookishly?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3108461367" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12490008237730334399">The Japanese Lover was a solid disappointment. I have had it on my shelves for a while, and I'd noticed some negative reviews during this time, so I suppose I purposely left it waiting, until recently. I was expecting SO much more, but instead, I received a flat romance that failed to conjure any kind of emotion in me.<br/><br/>The plot seemingly had some structure to it, but within this structure, were themes and words that were supposed to make the reader FEEL something. The only emotion I felt whilst r</span>
  <span id="freeText12490008237730334399" style="display:none">The Japanese Lover was a solid disappointment. I have had it on my shelves for a while, and I'd noticed some negative reviews during this time, so I suppose I purposely left it waiting, until recently. I was expecting SO much more, but instead, I received a flat romance that failed to conjure any kind of emotion in me.<br /><br />The plot seemingly had some structure to it, but within this structure, were themes and words that were supposed to make the reader FEEL something. The only emotion I felt whilst reading this, was irritation. <br /><br />If you're looking for characters with any depth, don't trouble yourself with this book, as these characters were paper thin. Sure, there were plenty of characters to go around, but none were developed to the standard of what I would expect, and certainly not to the standard of providing me with unforgettable characters, that I might feel warm inside when I think about.<br /><br />I like stories that trample on my heart, and one's that are able to make me flip five pages before I take a breath. It is like Allende didn't want to offend anyone, and played the entire novel safe, but by doing this, she has produced a tedious novel, with disjointed characters, and a soporific storyline. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12490008237730334399" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Although her new novel takes place in what we used to call an old folks’ home, “The Japanese Lover” is animated by the same lush spirit that has sold 65 million copies of her books around the world. While brushing aside the dismal expectations and hoary jokes about elderly people, she captures the real complexity and abiding p</span>
  <span id="freeText1694474555207883325" style="display:none">At 73, Isabel Allende is finally old enough to write about retirement with some personal authority, but there’s nothing retiring about her treatment of the twilight years. Although her new novel takes place in what we used to call an old folks’ home, “The Japanese Lover” is animated by the same lush spirit that has sold 65 million copies of her books around the world. While brushing aside the dismal expectations and hoary jokes about elderly people, she captures the real complexity and abiding passion of a long life.<br /><br />“The Japanese Lover” may be furnished with oxygen tanks and painkillers, but it blasts along like a turbocharged wheelchair. <span id="freeTextContainer8758953011989884446">Massively disappointing, especially for all the hype.<br/><br/>The reader is kept at an arm's length, so that, although many personal secrets and tragedies are continuously presented, there is no language that creates an emotional connection between reader and character.<br/><br/>Also written like the author researched historical and contemporary cultural touchstones, then used them like name-dropping. Didn't feel like the narrator had any personal interest in these events beyond an anthropological one.<br/><br/>Seth's voice</span>
  <span id="freeText8758953011989884446" style="display:none">Massively disappointing, especially for all the hype.<br /><br />The reader is kept at an arm's length, so that, although many personal secrets and tragedies are continuously presented, there is no language that creates an emotional connection between reader and character.<br /><br />Also written like the author researched historical and contemporary cultural touchstones, then used them like name-dropping. Didn't feel like the narrator had any personal interest in these events beyond an anthropological one.<br /><br />Seth's voice lacked believability, and Irina's life seemed to be constantly made-up on the spot. (How does she afford all the video games she plays, when so much of the focus is on her poverty/working multiple jobs/living in a shitty apartment??)</span>

<div id="review_1716766621" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1716766621" />
    <a title="Myrna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8789819-myrna"><img alt="Myrna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500745789p2/8789819.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1716766621?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Myrna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Myrna" href="/user/show/8789819-myrna">Myrna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25275996-the-japanese-lover">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8789819-myrna?shelf=kindle-ebook">kindle-ebook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1716766621" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13810410520105570775">Isabel Allende is such a skilled storyteller. This novel is full of surprises, slow disclosures, and containes loveable flawed characters. It also has some interesting yet sad historical pieces like the treatment of the Japenese on the west coast during WWII. <br/><br/><i>The Japanese Lover </i> is my first Allende book. I hear her other books are even better so this won't my last.<br/><br/>This was a buddy read with my friend Nita. It was fun discussing the book with her. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1449649240" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1449649240" />
    <a title="Jamise // Spines &amp; Vines" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13111928-jamise-spines-vines"><img alt="Jamise // Spines &amp; Vines" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1519748403p2/13111928.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jamise // Spines &amp; Vines" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jamise // Spines &amp; Vines" href="/user/show/13111928-jamise-spines-vines">Jamise // Spines &amp; Vines</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1449649240" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1285584340292321989">I was looking forward to starting 2016 with my first book by Isabel Allende. Unfortunately I'm disappointed as this book turned out to be quite blah. As a reader, it was easy to fall in sync with the pace of the story but I never became invested (or cared) about any of the characters. The story remained flat with only a few elements that sparked my interest very late in the book. Will I read another novel by this author? Absolutely! The House of The Spirits comes highly recommended. <br/><br/></span>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1322810300" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1322810300" />
    <a title="Dorie  - Cats&amp;Books :)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16912659-dorie---cats-books"><img alt="Dorie  - Cats&amp;Books :)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550077760p2/16912659.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1322810300?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dorie  - Cats&amp;Books :)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dorie  - Cats&amp;Books :)" href="/user/show/16912659-dorie---cats-books">Dorie  - Cats&amp;Books :)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16912659-dorie---cats-books?shelf=netgalley-books">netgalley-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16912659-dorie---cats-books?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1322810300" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6383194344438946049">I received an ARC of this book from NetGalley in exchange for an honest review.<br/><br/>I have long loved the poetic voice of Isabel Allende’s novels. A few of her recent novels left me not quite satisfied so I was very anxious to read The Japanese lover. In this book I feel as though she has returned to her very strong characters, with complicated but fully developed background history for all, not only the major players but some of the minor ones as well.<br/> <br/>The book is about loving, giving, forgiving and</span>
  <span id="freeText6383194344438946049" style="display:none">I received an ARC of this book from NetGalley in exchange for an honest review.<br /><br />I have long loved the poetic voice of Isabel Allende’s novels. A few of her recent novels left me not quite satisfied so I was very anxious to read The Japanese lover. In this book I feel as though she has returned to her very strong characters, with complicated but fully developed background history for all, not only the major players but some of the minor ones as well.<br /> <br />The book is about loving, giving, forgiving and allowing those you love to have their own space, their own identities, their own secrets. The novel is narrated in the third person. The first half does spend a lot of time on the Belasco and Fukuda family history but it is essential in setting up the main characters in the book. It certainly is uncomfortable being reminded how we treated even American born Japanese and their family with “relocating” them into camps and the trials they faced there. Even after release the Japanese were not welcomed back into the community. It was only because of the Belasco’s friendship and generosity that the Fukuda family were able to re-establish their farm.<br /> <br />The relationship between Alma and Ichimei is a complicated one and goes through many changes throughout their time together. For Alma he was her one true love but she found happiness, security and friendship in Nathanial. Alma is a very talented artist and uses her art as an outlet for her passions. Ichimei puts everything he has into the land. <br /> <br />Seth, Alma’s grandson, and Irina, a woman hired to help Alma unclutter her life, work together to help Alma record her memoirs. There are beautifully worded love letters from Ichimei to Alma which she reads again and again. Irina in particular has a very painful history that she is learning to live with.<br /><br />This is very much a love story but with so much history of the families it is definitely historical fiction. I enjoyed this read however Daughter of Fortune and Portrait in Sepia remain my favorites, when Allende writes about her homeland of Chile<br />. <br />I would recommend this one to book clubs as there is lots for discussion and just to anyone who wants to read a well written, beautiful novel.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6383194344438946049" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1488096829" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1488096829" />
    <a title="Camie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7399266-camie"><img alt="Camie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571025937p2/7399266.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1488096829?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Camie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Camie" href="/user/show/7399266-camie">Camie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1488096829" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16027448244279819529">Allende's sweeping tale of forbidden love and loss, is really two stories. Alma is sent from Poland to live safely in San Francisco with her relatives in 1938 when Natzi threats lead the world into war. Decades later Irina, a young Moldavian care worker, fleeing a devastating past of her own , begins working at the eccentric care center called Lark house where the elderly Alma now resides. It's here that their paths meet and where they will both share their histories some of which ( Alma's) span</span>
  <span id="freeText16027448244279819529" style="display:none">Allende's sweeping tale of forbidden love and loss, is really two stories. Alma is sent from Poland to live safely in San Francisco with her relatives in 1938 when Natzi threats lead the world into war. Decades later Irina, a young Moldavian care worker, fleeing a devastating past of her own , begins working at the eccentric care center called Lark house where the elderly Alma now resides. It's here that their paths meet and where they will both share their histories some of which ( Alma's) span years and continents. It was a time when certain things were neither talked about or done. But the war and the internment of Japanese Americans , who were viewed as the enemy after the attack on Pearl Harbor, play a big part in secrets that have been kept for 60 years. <br />I had heard this newest book by Allende was not her best , but enjoying historical fiction as I do, I found it quite interesting. Sometimes when everything is lost ..love may be all that endures. 4 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="16027448244279819529" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('/W5sZip1jgmrqb10eF3P9wZBt6ztMPGtLZ66GjkqU3scScOI3a9eIqqy5GK8OYS4N/L7horwWYjl6xLuHDunHw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1bxRLGb8uhGQrZEXjWrMl6q5lamp13SjLhE7bULSB7Q0m/7CkSZqOpG2yAFJDofYmwrZg84X3IbmZJOZZ8Pz0A==')})
  }

Salvar el fuego retrata dos Méxicos completamente escindidos uno del otro, donde Marina, que pertenece a la clase social más alta, se vincula con un hombre al extremo de la sociedad. Esta es una novela que retrata las contradicciones de un país y las contradicciones más hondas de la naturaleza humana. Es una novela de amor y es una novela que al final termina por brindar esperanza. «Una novela polifónica que narra con intensidad y con excepcional dinamismo una historia de violencia en el México contemporáneo donde el amor y la redención aún son posibles. El autor se sirve tantode una extraordinaria fuerza visual como de la recreación y reinvención del lenguaje coloquial para lograr una obra de inquietante verosimilitud. Los distintos planos narrativos tienen como hilo conductor el cuerpo humano, motivo de celebración y expuesto a numerosos excesos.»Del acta del jurado La crítica ha dicho:«El mexicano Guillermo Arriaga no es solo un escritor de la gran pantalla sino un narrador de raza, cuyas obsesiones vitales dejan honda huella en el lector.»Matías Néspolo, El Mundo «Un autor absolutamente único.»Guadalupe Nettel «Uno de los autores contemporáneos más potentes, intensos y originales de la literatura en idioma español.»El Exprés (México) «Arriaga demuestra ser gran director a la par que gran escritor.»Roberto Piorno, Guía del Ocio «Con sensibilidad extrema y poderío visual, enlazando con coherencia personajes y situaciones que inicialmente parecen no guardar relación [...], Arriaga demuestra que, además de un espléndido guionista, también es un buen director.»Carlos Boyero, El País «El Salvaje es uno de los mejores libros que he leído, no solo en este sino en los últimos años.»Santiago Gamboa «La presencia ominosa de la muerte; el amor o la pasión que todo lo crea y, por encima, la fuerza irrefrenable de la vida que arrastra todo consigo en su prepotencia arrolladora. <span id="freeTextContainer2931383171529889054">Isabel Allende Llona is a Chilean-American novelist. Allende, who writes in the "magic realism" tradition, is considered one of the first successful women novelists in Latin America. She has written novels based in part on her own experiences, often focusing on the experiences of women, weaving myth and realism together. She has lectured and done extensive book tours and has taught literature at s</span>
  <span id="freeText2931383171529889054" style="display:none">Isabel Allende Llona is a Chilean-American novelist. Allende, who writes in the "magic realism" tradition, is considered one of the first successful women novelists in Latin America. She has written novels based in part on her own experiences, often focusing on the experiences of women, weaving myth and realism together. She has lectured and done extensive book tours and has taught literature at several US colleges. She currently resides in California with her husband. Allende adopted U.S. citizenship in 2003.<br /><br /></span>
